#  8.6. Insertion Sort and Array Mutation[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=insertion-sort-mutation "Permalink")
While insertion sort does not have the optimal worst-case time complexity for a sorting algorithm, it still has a number of useful properties:
  * It is simple and straightforward to implement and understand
  * It is an in-place algorithm, requiring no additional space to run
  * It is a stable sort
  * It is fast when the input is already almost sorted


In-place algorithms are particularly useful in Lean due to the way it manages memory. In some cases, operations that would normally copy an array can be optimized into mutation. This includes swapping elements in an array.
Most languages and run-time systems with automatic memory management, including JavaScript, the JVM, and .NET, use tracing garbage collection. When memory needs to be reclaimed, the system starts at a number of _roots_ (such as the call stack and global values) and then determines which values can be reached by recursively chasing pointers. Any values that can't be reached are deallocated, freeing memory.
Reference counting is an alternative to tracing garbage collection that is used by a number of languages, including Python, Swift, and Lean. In a system with reference counting, each object in memory has a field that tracks how many references there are to it. When a new reference is established, the counter is incremented. When a reference ceases to exist, the counter is decremented. When the counter reaches zero, the object is immediately deallocated.
Reference counting has one major disadvantage compared to a tracing garbage collector: circular references can lead to memory leaks. If object `AAA` references object `BBB` , and object `BBB` references object `AAA`, they will never be deallocated, even if nothing else in the program references either `AAA` or `BBB`. Circular references result either from uncontrolled recursion or from mutable references. Because Lean supports neither, it is impossible to construct circular references.
Reference counting means that the Lean runtime system's primitives for allocating and deallocating data structures can check whether a reference count is about to fall to zero, and re-use an existing object instead of allocating a new one. This is particularly important when working with large arrays.
An implementation of insertion sort for Lean arrays should satisfy the following criteria:
  1. Lean should accept the function without a `partial` annotation
  2. If passed an array to which there are no other references, it should modify the array in-place rather than allocating a new one


The first criterion is easy to check: if Lean accepts the definition, then it is satisfied. The second, however, requires a means of testing it. Lean provides a built-in function called `[dbgTraceIfShared](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Run-Time-Code/Reference-Counting/#dbgTraceIfShared "Documentation for dbgTraceIfShared in Lean Language Reference")` with the following signature:
``[dbgTraceIfShared.{u}](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Run-Time-Code/Reference-Counting/#dbgTraceIfShared "Documentation for dbgTraceIfShared in Lean Language Reference") {α : Type u} (s : [String](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Strings/#String___mk "Documentation for String in Lean Language Reference")) (a : α) : α`[#check](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Interacting-with-Lean/#Lean___Parser___Command___check "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") [dbgTraceIfShared](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Run-Time-Code/Reference-Counting/#dbgTraceIfShared "Documentation for dbgTraceIfShared in Lean Language Reference")`
```
[dbgTraceIfShared.{u}](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Run-Time-Code/Reference-Counting/#dbgTraceIfShared "Documentation for dbgTraceIfShared in Lean Language Reference") {α : Type u} (s : [String](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Strings/#String___mk "Documentation for String in Lean Language Reference")) (a : α) : α
```

It takes a string and a value as arguments, and prints a message that uses the string to standard error if the value has more than one reference, returning the value. This is not, strictly speaking, a pure function. However, it is intended to be used only during development to check that a function is in fact able to re-use memory rather than allocating and copying.
When learning to use `[dbgTraceIfShared](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Run-Time-Code/Reference-Counting/#dbgTraceIfShared "Documentation for dbgTraceIfShared in Lean Language Reference")`, it's important to know that `#eval` will report that many more values are shared than in compiled code. This can be confusing. It's important to build an executable with `lake` rather than experimenting in an editor.
Insertion sort consists of two loops. The outer loop moves a pointer from left to right across the array to be sorted. After each iteration, the region of the array to the left of the pointer is sorted, while the region to the right may not yet be sorted. The inner loop takes the element pointed to by the pointer and moves it to the left until the appropriate location has been found and the loop invariant has been restored. In other words, each iteration inserts the next element of the array into the appropriate location in the sorted region.
##  8.6.1. The Inner Loop[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=inner-insertion-sort-loop "Permalink")
The inner loop of insertion sort can be implemented as a tail-recursive function that takes the array and the index of the element being inserted as arguments. The element being inserted is repeatedly swapped with the element to its left until either the element to the left is smaller or the beginning of the array is reached. The inner loop is structurally recursive on the `[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")` that is inside the `[Fin](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Finite-Natural-Numbers/#Fin___mk "Documentation for Fin in Lean Language Reference")` used to index into the array:
`def insertSorted [[Ord](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#Ord___mk "Documentation for Ord in Lean Language Reference") α] (arr : [Array](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___mk "Documentation for Array in Lean Language Reference") α) (i : (arr.[swap](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___swap "Documentation for Array.swap in Lean Language Reference") i' (↑i) this ⋯).[size](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___size "Documentation for Array.size in Lean Language Reference") [simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [*]All goals completed! 🐙⟩`
If the index `i` is `0`, then the element being inserted into the sorted region has reached the beginning of the region and is the smallest. If the index is `i' + 1`, then the element at `i'` should be compared to the element at `i`. Note that while `i` is a `[Fin](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Finite-Natural-Numbers/#Fin___mk "Documentation for Fin in Lean Language Reference") arr.[size](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___size "Documentation for Array.size in Lean Language Reference")`, `i'` is just a `[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")` because it results from the `[val](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Finite-Natural-Numbers/#Fin___mk "Documentation for Fin.val in Lean Language Reference")` field of `i`. Nonetheless, the proof automation used for checking array index notation includes a solver for linear integer arithmetic, so `i'` is automatically usable as an index.
The two elements are looked up and compared. If the element to the left is less than or equal to the element being inserted, then the loop is finished and the invariant has been restored. If the element to the left is greater than the element being inserted, then the elements are swapped and the inner loop begins again. `[Array.swap](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___swap "Documentation for Array.swap in Lean Language Reference")` takes both of its indices as `[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")`s, using the same tactics as array indexing behind the scenes to ensure that they are in bounds.
Nonetheless, the `[Fin](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Finite-Natural-Numbers/#Fin___mk "Documentation for Fin in Lean Language Reference")` used for the recursive call needs a proof that `i'` is in bounds for the result of swapping two elements. The `[simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` tactic's database contains the fact that swapping two elements of an array doesn't change its size, and the `[*]` argument instructs it to additionally use the assumption introduced by `have`. Omitting the `have`-expression with the proof that `i' < arr.[size](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___size "Documentation for Array.size in Lean Language Reference")` reveals the following goal:

```
unsolved goals
α:Type ?u.7inst✝:[Ord](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#Ord___mk "Documentation for Ord in Lean Language Reference") αarr:[Array](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___mk "Documentation for Array in Lean Language Reference") αi:[Fin](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Finite-Natural-Numbers/#Fin___mk "Documentation for Fin in Lean Language Reference") arr.[size](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___size "Documentation for Array.size in Lean Language Reference")i':[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")isLt✝:i' [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") 1 [<](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt in Lean Language Reference") arr.[size](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___size "Documentation for Array.size in Lean Language Reference")⊢ i' [<](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt in Lean Language Reference") arr.[size](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___size "Documentation for Array.size in Lean Language Reference")
```

##  8.6.2. The Outer Loop[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=outer-insertion-sort-loop "Permalink")
The outer loop of insertion sort moves the pointer from left to right, invoking `insertSorted` at each iteration to insert the element at the pointer into the correct position in the array. The basic form of the loop resembles the implementation of `Array.map`:
`def `fail to show termination for   insertionSortLoop with errors failed to infer structural recursion: Not considering parameter α of insertionSortLoop:   it is unchanged in the recursive calls Not considering parameter #2 of insertionSortLoop:   it is unchanged in the recursive calls Cannot use parameter arr:   the type [Array](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___mk "Documentation for Array in Lean Language Reference") α does not have a `.brecOn` recursor Cannot use parameter i:   failed to eliminate recursive application     insertionSortLoop (insertSorted arr [⟨](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Finite-Natural-Numbers/#Fin___mk "Documentation for Fin.mk in Lean Language Reference")i[,](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Finite-Natural-Numbers/#Fin___mk "Documentation for Fin.mk in Lean Language Reference") h[⟩](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Finite-Natural-Numbers/#Fin___mk "Documentation for Fin.mk in Lean Language Reference")) [(](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference")i [+](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference") 1[)](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd in Lean Language Reference")   Could not find a decreasing measure. While Lean can prove that a `[Nat](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat in Lean Language Reference")` that increases towards a constant bound at each iteration leads to a terminating function, this function has no constant bound because the array is replaced with the result of calling `insertSorted` at each iteration.
Before constructing the termination proof, it can be convenient to test the definition with a `partial` modifier to make sure that it returns the expected answers:
`partial def insertionSortLoop [[Ord](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#Ord___mk "Documentation for Ord in Lean Language Reference") α] (arr : ###  8.6.2.1. Termination[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=insertionSortLoop-termination "Permalink")
Once again, the function terminates because the difference between the index and the size of the array being processed decreases on each recursive call. This time, however, Lean does not accept the `termination_by`:
`def insertionSortLoop [[Ord](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#Ord___mk "Documentation for Ord in Lean Language Reference") α] (arr : The problem is that Lean has no way to know that `insertSorted` returns an array that's the same size as the one it is passed. In order to prove that `insertionSortLoop` terminates, it is necessary to first prove that `insertSorted` doesn't change the size of the array. Copying the unproved termination condition from the error message to the function and “proving” it with `[sorry](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#sorry "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` allows the function to be temporarily accepted:
``declaration uses 'sorry'`def `declaration uses 'sorry'``declaration uses 'sorry'``declaration uses 'sorry'``declaration uses 'sorry'`insertionSortLoop ```

Because `insertSorted` is structurally recursive on the index of the element being inserted, the proof should be by induction on the index. In the base case, the array is returned unchanged, so its length certainly does not change. For the inductive step, the induction hypothesis is that a recursive call on the next smaller index will not change the length of the array. There are two cases two consider: either the element has been fully inserted into the sorted region and the array is returned unchanged, in which case the length is also unchanged, or the element is swapped with the next one before the recursive call. However, swapping two elements in an array doesn't change the size of it, and the induction hypothesis states that the recursive call with the next index returns an array that's the same size as its argument. Thus, the size remains unchanged.
Translating this English-language theorem statement to Lean and proceeding using the techniques from this chapter is enough to prove the base case and make progress in the inductive step:
`theorem insert_sorted_size_eq [[Ord](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#Ord___mk "Documentation for Ord in Lean Language Reference") α] (arr : [Array](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___mk "Documentation for Array in Lean Language Reference") α) (i : [Fin](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Finite-Natural-Numbers/#Fin___mk "Documentation for Fin in Lean Language Reference") The simplification using `insertSorted` in the inductive step revealed the pattern match in `insertSorted`:

When faced with a goal that includes `if` or `match`, the `[split](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#split "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` tactic (not to be confused with the `splitList` function used in the definition of merge sort) replaces the goal with one new goal for each path of control flow:

Because it typically doesn't matter _how_ a statement was proved, but only _that_ it was proved, proofs in Lean's output are typically replaced by `⋯`. Additionally, each new goal has an assumption that indicates which branch led to that goal, named `heq✝` in this case:

Rather than write proofs for both simple cases, adding `<;> [try](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#try "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference") [rfl](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rfl "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` after `[split](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#split "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` causes the two straightforward cases to disappear immediately, leaving only a single goal:

```

Unfortunately, the induction hypothesis is not strong enough to prove this goal. The induction hypothesis states that calling `insertSorted` on `arr` leaves the size unchanged, but the proof goal is to show that the result of the recursive call with the result of swapping leaves the size unchanged. Successfully completing the proof requires an induction hypothesis that works for _any_ array that is passed to `insertSorted` together with the smaller index as an argument
It is possible to get a strong induction hypothesis by using the `generalizing` option to the `[induction](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#induction "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` tactic. This option brings additional assumptions from the context into the statement that's used to generate the base case, the induction hypothesis, and the goal to be shown in the inductive step. Generalizing over `arr` leads to a stronger hypothesis:

In the resulting goal, `arr` is now part of a “for all” statement in the inductive hypothesis:

However, this whole proof is beginning to get unmanageable. The next step would be to introduce a variable standing for the length of the result of swapping, show that it is equal to `arr.[size](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___size "Documentation for Array.size in Lean Language Reference")`, and then show that this variable is also equal to the length of the array that results from the recursive call. These equality statements can then be chained together to prove the goal. It's much easier, however, to use functional induction:
`theorem insert_sorted_size_eq [[Ord](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#Ord___mk "Documentation for Ord in Lean Language Reference") α]     (arr : [Array](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___mk "Documentation for Array in Lean Language Reference") α) (i : [Fin](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Finite-Natural-Numbers/#Fin___mk "Documentation for Fin in Lean Language Reference") arr.[size](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___size "Documentation for Array.size in Lean Language Reference")) :     (insertSorted arr i).[size](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___size "Documentation for Array.size in Lean Language Reference") = arr.[size](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___size "Documentation for Array.size in Lean Language Reference") := byα:Type αi:[Fin](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Finite-Natural-Numbers/#Fin___mk "Documentation for Fin in Lean Language Reference") The first goal is the case for index `0`. Here, the array is not modified, so proving that its size is unmodified will not require any complicated steps:

```
unsolved goals
case1α:Type u_1inst✝:[Ord](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#Ord___mk "Documentation for Ord in Lean Language Reference") αarr✝ arr:[Array](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___mk "Documentation for Array in Lean Language Reference") αisLt:0 [<](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt in Lean Language Reference") arr.[size](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___size "Documentation for Array.size in Lean Language Reference")⊢ arr.[size](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___size "Documentation for Array.size in Lean Language Reference") [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference") arr.[size](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___size "Documentation for Array.size in Lean Language Reference")
```

The next two goals are the same, and cover the `[.lt](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#Ordering___lt "Documentation for Ordering.lt in Lean Language Reference")` and `[.eq](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#Ordering___lt "Documentation for Ordering.eq in Lean Language Reference")` cases for the element comparison. The local assumptions `isLt` and `isEq` will allow the correct branch of the `[match](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference")` to be selected:

```

arr[[](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#GetElem___mk "Documentation for GetElem.getElem in Lean Language Reference")i[]](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#GetElem___mk "Documentation for GetElem.getElem in Lean Language Reference") Reference")[,](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Finite-Natural-Numbers/#Fin___mk "Documentation for Fin.mk in Lean Language Reference")     | [Ordering.lt](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#Ordering___lt "Documentation for Ordering.lt in Lean Language Reference") => arr
    | [Ordering.eq](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#Ordering___lt "Documentation for Ordering.eq in Lean Language Reference") => arr
    | [Ordering.gt](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#Ordering___lt "Documentation for Ordering.gt in Lean Language Reference") => insertSorted (arr.[swap](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___swap "Documentation for Array.swap in Lean Language Reference") i (↑[⟨](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Finite-Natural-Numbers/#Fin___mk "Documentation for Fin.mk in Lean Language Reference")i.[succ](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ in Lean Language Reference")[,](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Finite-Natural-Numbers/#Fin___mk "Documentation for Fin.mk in Lean Language Reference") isLt[⟩](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Finite-Natural-Numbers/#Fin___mk "Documentation for Fin.mk in Lean Language Reference")) this ⋯) [⟨](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Finite-Natural-Numbers/#Fin___mk "Documentation for Fin.mk in Lean Language Reference")i[,](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Finite-Natural-Numbers/#Fin___mk "Documentation for Fin.mk in Lean Language Reference") ⋯[⟩](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Finite-Natural-Numbers/#Fin___mk "Documentation for Fin.mk in Lean Language Reference")).[size](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___size "Documentation for Array.size in Lean Language Reference") [=](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq in Lean Language Reference")
  arr.[size](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___size "Documentation for Array.size in Lean Language Reference")
```

In the final case, once the `[match](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference")` is reduced, there will be some work left to do to prove that the next step of the insertion preserves the size of the array. In particular, the induction hypothesis states that the size of the next step is equal to the size of the result of the swap, but the desired conclusion is that it's equal to the size of the original array:

```

The Lean library includes the theorem `Array.size_swap`, which states that swapping two elements of an array doesn't change its size. By default, `[grind](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#grind "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` doesn't use this fact, but once instructed to do so, it can take care of all four cases:
`theorem insert_sorted_size_eq [[Ord](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#Ord___mk "Documentation for Ord in Lean Language Reference") α]     (arr : [Array](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___mk "Documentation for Array in Lean Language Reference") α) (i : [Fin](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Finite-Natural-Numbers/#Fin___mk "Documentation for Fin in Lean Language Reference") i).[size](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___size "Documentation for Array.size in Lean Language Reference") = This proof can now be used to replace the `[sorry](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#sorry "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` in `insertionSortLoop`. In particular, this theorem allows `[grind](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#grind "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` to succeed:
`def insertionSortLoop [[Ord](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#Ord___mk "Documentation for Ord in Lean Language Reference") α] (arr : [Array](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___mk "Documentation for Array in Lean Language Reference") α) (i : [if](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Terms/Conditionals/#termDepIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") h : i < [then](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Terms/Conditionals/#termDepIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference")     have : (insertSorted arr ⟨i, h⟩).[size](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___size "Documentation for Array.size in Lean Language Reference") - (i + 1) < insertionSortLoop (insertSorted arr ⟨i, h⟩) (i + 1)   [else](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Terms/Conditionals/#termDepIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference")     arr termination_by arr.[size](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___size "Documentation for Array.size in Lean Language Reference") - i`
##  8.6.3. The Driver Function[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=insertion-sort-driver-function "Permalink")
Insertion sort itself calls `insertionSortLoop`, initializing the index that demarcates the sorted region of the array from the unsorted region to `0`:
`def insertionSort [[Ord](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#Ord___mk "Documentation for Ord in Lean Language Reference") α] (arr : [Array](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___mk "Documentation for Array in Lean Language Reference") α) : [Array](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___mk "Documentation for Array in Lean Language Reference") α :=    insertionSortLoop arr 0`
A few quick tests show the function is at least not blatantly wrong:
``[#[](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___toArray "Documentation for List.toArray in Lean Language Reference")1[,](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons in Lean Language Reference") 3[,](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons in Lean Language Reference") 4[,](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons in Lean Language Reference") 7[]](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___toArray "Documentation for List.toArray in Lean Language Reference")`[#eval](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Interacting-with-Lean/#Lean___Parser___Command___eval "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference") insertionSort #[3, 1, 7, 4]`
```
[#[](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___toArray "Documentation for List.toArray in Lean Language Reference")1[,](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons in Lean Language Reference") 3[,](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons in Lean Language Reference") 4[,](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons in Lean Language Reference") 7[]](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___toArray "Documentation for List.toArray in Lean Language Reference")
```

##  8.6.4. Is This Really Insertion Sort?[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=insertion-sort-in-place "Permalink")
Insertion sort is _defined_ to be an in-place sorting algorithm. What makes it useful, despite its quadratic worst-case run time, is that it is a stable sorting algorithm that doesn't allocate extra space and that handles almost-sorted data efficiently. If each iteration of the inner loop allocated a new array, then the algorithm wouldn't _really_ be insertion sort.
Lean's array operations, such as `[Array.set](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___set "Documentation for Array.set in Lean Language Reference")` and `[Array.swap](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___swap "Documentation for Array.swap in Lean Language Reference")`, check whether the array in question has a reference count that is greater than one. If so, then the array is visible to multiple parts of the code, which means that it must be copied. Otherwise, Lean would no longer be a pure functional language. However, when the reference count is exactly one, there are no other potential observers of the value. In these cases, the array primitives mutate the array in place. What other parts of the program don't know can't hurt them.
Lean's proof logic works at the level of pure functional programs, not the underlying implementation. This means that the best way to discover whether a program unnecessarily copies data is to test it. Adding calls to `[dbgTraceIfShared](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Run-Time-Code/Reference-Counting/#dbgTraceIfShared "Documentation for dbgTraceIfShared in Lean Language Reference")` at each point where mutation is desired causes the provided message to be printed to `stderr` when the value in question has more than one reference.
Insertion sort has precisely one place that is at risk of copying rather than mutating: the call to `[Array.swap](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___swap "Documentation for Array.swap in Lean Language Reference")`. Replacing `arr.[swap](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___swap "Documentation for Array.swap in Lean Language Reference") i' i` with `([dbgTraceIfShared](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Run-Time-Code/Reference-Counting/#dbgTraceIfShared "Documentation for dbgTraceIfShared in Lean Language Reference") "array to swap" arr).[swap](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___swap "Documentation for Array.swap in Lean Language Reference") i' i` causes the program to emit `shared RC array to swap` whenever it is unable to mutate the array. However, this change to the program changes the proofs as well, because now there's a call to an additional function. Adding a local assumption that `[dbgTraceIfShared](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Run-Time-Code/Reference-Counting/#dbgTraceIfShared "Documentation for dbgTraceIfShared in Lean Language Reference")` preserves the length of its argument and adding it to some calls to `[simp](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic in Lean Language Reference")` is enough to fix the program and proofs.
The complete instrumented code for insertion sort is:

termination_by arr.[size](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___size "Documentation for Array.size in Lean Language Reference") - i  def insertionSort [[Ord](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#Ord___mk "Documentation for Ord in Lean Language Reference") α] (arr : [Array](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___mk "Documentation for Array in Lean Language Reference") α) : [Array](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___mk "Documentation for Array in Lean Language Reference") α :=   insertionSortLoop arr 0`
A bit of cleverness is required to check whether the instrumentation actually works. First off, the Lean compiler aggressively optimizes function calls away when all their arguments are known at compile time. Simply writing a program that applies `insertionSort` to a large array is not sufficient, because the resulting compiled code may contain only the sorted array as a constant. The easiest way to ensure that the compiler doesn't optimize away the sorting routine is to read the array from `stdin`. Secondly, the compiler performs dead code elimination. Adding extra `let`s to the program won't necessarily result in more references in running code if the `let`-bound variables are never used. To ensure that the extra reference is not eliminated entirely, it's important to ensure that the extra reference is somehow used.
The first step in testing the instrumentation is to write `getLines`, which reads an array of lines from standard input:
`def getLines : [IO](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/IO/Logical-Model/#IO "Documentation for IO in Lean Language Reference") ([Array](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___mk "Documentation for Array in Lean Language Reference") [String](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Strings/#String___mk "Documentation for String in Lean Language Reference")) := [do](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Functors___-Monads-and--do--Notation/Syntax/#Lean___Parser___Term___do "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference")   let stdin ← [IO.getStdin](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/IO/Files___-File-Handles___-and-Streams/#IO___getStdin "Documentation for IO.getStdin in Lean Language Reference")   let mut lines : [Array](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___mk "Documentation for Array in Lean Language Reference") [String](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Strings/#String___mk "Documentation for String in Lean Language Reference") := #[]   let mut currLine ← stdin.[getLine](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/IO/Files___-File-Handles___-and-Streams/#IO___FS___Stream___mk "Documentation for IO.FS.Stream.getLine in Lean Language Reference")   while !currLine.[isEmpty](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Strings/#String___isEmpty "Documentation for String.isEmpty in Lean Language Reference") do      -- Drop trailing newline:     lines := lines.[push](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___push "Documentation for Array.push in Lean Language Reference") (currLine.[dropRight](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Strings/#String___dropRight "Documentation for String.dropRight in Lean Language Reference") 1)     currLine ← stdin.[getLine](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/IO/Files___-File-Handles___-and-Streams/#IO___FS___Stream___mk "Documentation for IO.FS.Stream.getLine in Lean Language Reference")   [pure](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Functors___-Monads-and--do--Notation/#Pure___mk "Documentation for Pure.pure in Lean Language Reference") lines`
`[IO.FS.Stream.getLine](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/IO/Files___-File-Handles___-and-Streams/#IO___FS___Stream___mk "Documentation for IO.FS.Stream.getLine in Lean Language Reference")` returns a complete line of text, including the trailing newline. It returns `""` when the end-of-file marker has been reached.
Next, two separate `main` routines are needed. Both read the array to be sorted from standard input, ensuring that the calls to `insertionSort` won't be replaced by their return values at compile time. Both then print to the console, ensuring that the calls to `insertionSort` won't be optimized away entirely. One of them prints only the sorted array, while the other prints both the sorted array and the original array. The second function should trigger a warning that `[Array.swap](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___swap "Documentation for Array.swap in Lean Language Reference")` had to allocate a new array:
`def mainUnique : [IO](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/IO/Logical-Model/#IO "Documentation for IO in Lean Language Reference") [Unit](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/The-Unit-Type/#Unit "Documentation for Unit in Lean Language Reference") := [do](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Functors___-Monads-and--do--Notation/Syntax/#Lean___Parser___Term___do "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference")   let lines ← getLines   for line in insertionSort lines do     [IO.println](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/IO/Console-Output/#IO___println "Documentation for IO.println in Lean Language Reference") line  def mainShared : [IO](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/IO/Logical-Model/#IO "Documentation for IO in Lean Language Reference") [Unit](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/The-Unit-Type/#Unit "Documentation for Unit in Lean Language Reference") := [do](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Functors___-Monads-and--do--Notation/Syntax/#Lean___Parser___Term___do "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference")   let lines ← getLines   [IO.println](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/IO/Console-Output/#IO___println "Documentation for IO.println in Lean Language Reference") "--- Sorted lines: ---"   for line in insertionSort lines do     [IO.println](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/IO/Console-Output/#IO___println "Documentation for IO.println in Lean Language Reference") line    [IO.println](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/IO/Console-Output/#IO___println "Documentation for IO.println in Lean Language Reference") ""   [IO.println](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/IO/Console-Output/#IO___println "Documentation for IO.println in Lean Language Reference") "--- Original data: ---"   for line in lines do     [IO.println](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/IO/Console-Output/#IO___println "Documentation for IO.println in Lean Language Reference") line`
The actual `main` simply selects one of the two main actions based on the provided command-line arguments:
`def main (args : [List](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List in Lean Language Reference") [String](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Strings/#String___mk "Documentation for String in Lean Language Reference")) : [IO](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/IO/Logical-Model/#IO "Documentation for IO in Lean Language Reference") [UInt32](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Fixed-Precision-Integers/#UInt32___ofBitVec "Documentation for UInt32 in Lean Language Reference") := [do](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Functors___-Monads-and--do--Notation/Syntax/#Lean___Parser___Term___do "Documentation for syntax in Lean Language Reference")   match args with   | ["--shared"] => [mainShared](Programming___-Proving___-and-Performance/Insertion-Sort-and-Array-Mutation/#mainShared "Definition of example"); [pure](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Functors___-Monads-and--do--Notation/#Pure___mk "Documentation for Pure.pure in Lean Language Reference") 0   | ["--unique"] => [mainUnique](Programming___-Proving___-and-Performance/Insertion-Sort-and-Array-Mutation/#mainUnique "Definition of example"); [pure](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Functors___-Monads-and--do--Notation/#Pure___mk "Documentation for Pure.pure in Lean Language Reference") 0   | _ =>     [IO.println](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/IO/Console-Output/#IO___println "Documentation for IO.println in Lean Language Reference") "Expected single argument, either \"--shared\" or \"--unique\""     [pure](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Functors___-Monads-and--do--Notation/#Pure___mk "Documentation for Pure.pure in Lean Language Reference") 1`
Running it with no arguments produces the expected usage information:
`sort``Expected single argument, either "--shared" or "--unique" `
The file `test-data` contains the following rocks:
File: `test-data``schist``feldspar``diorite``pumice``obsidian``shale``gneiss``marble``flint`
Using the instrumented insertion sort on these rocks results them being printed in alphabetical order:
`sort --unique < test-data``diorite feldspar flint gneiss marble obsidian pumice schist shale `
However, the version in which a reference is retained to the original array results in a notification on `stderr` (namely, `shared RC array to swap`) from the first call to `[Array.swap](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___swap "Documentation for Array.swap in Lean Language Reference")`:
`sort --shared < test-data``--- Sorted lines: --- diorite feldspar flint gneiss marble obsidian pumice schist shale  --- Original data: --- schist feldspar diorite pumice obsidian shale gneiss marble flint ``shared RC array to swap `
The fact that only a single `shared RC` notification appears means that the array is copied only once. This is because the copy that results from the call to `[Array.swap](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___swap "Documentation for Array.swap in Lean Language Reference")` is itself unique, so no further copies need to be made. In an imperative language, subtle bugs can result from forgetting to explicitly copy an array before passing it by reference. When running `sort --shared`, the array is copied as needed to preserve the pure functional meaning of Lean programs, but no more.
##  8.6.5. Other Opportunities for Mutation
The use of mutation instead of copying when references are unique is not limited to array update operators. Lean also attempts to “recycle” constructors whose reference counts are about to fall to zero, reusing them instead of allocating new data. This means, for instance, that `[List.map](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.26.0/Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___map "Documentation for List.map in Lean Language Reference")` will mutate a linked list in place, at least in cases when nobody could possibly notice. One of the most important steps in optimizing hot loops in Lean code is making sure that the data being modified is not referred to from multiple locations.
##  8.6.6. Exercises[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=insertion-sort-exercises "Permalink")
  * Write a function that reverses arrays. Test that if the input array has a reference count of one, then your function does not allocate a new array.
  * Implement either merge sort or quicksort for arrays. Prove that your implementation terminates, and test that it doesn't allocate more arrays than expected. This is a challenging exercise!
